## Section 2: Executive Summary

This full-stack food delivery platform (FastAPI + React/TypeScript) produced 1,963 actionable findings from 2,388 raw detections (425 auto-suppressed). The dominant volume — roughly 70 % of findings — consists of low-severity Python typing modernisations (UP035/UP045/UP006) and line-length issues that are all safe auto-fixes. More concerning are three distinct high-severity clusters: a hardcoded fallback JWT SECRET_KEY that silently applies if the env-var is absent, Dockerfile security issues (running as root, recursive COPY without a .dockerignore), and approximately 900 ESLint no-undef findings that expose a missing browser-environment declaration in the ESLint/TypeScript configuration — a systemic misconfiguration producing massive false-positive noise rather than real bugs, but still indicative of a broken frontend linting pipeline. Compounding these is SonarQube-reported 0.0 % test coverage alongside unused parameters in all three payment gateway stubs (_gateway_authorize, _gateway_capture, _gateway_refund), strongly suggesting the payment integration is entirely mocked and not production-ready. Several service functions also far exceed cognitive-complexity thresholds (assign_delivery_agent at 40, list_restaurants at 33), increasing defect probability in the core delivery and browse flows.

## Section 4: Static Analysis Findings

_A tool detecting a pattern (confidence: Very High) is not the same as that pattern being a real, actionable problem - those are different questions. Findings below are grouped by `bucket`: 4.1 Safe Auto-Fix (deterministic, no reasoning required), 4.2 AI-Suggested Refactoring (needs reasoning, conditional auto-fix), 4.3 Manual Review Required (business logic / security - never auto-refactor), 4.4 Suppressed (auto-filtered false positives, with why)._

| CR-1963 | 6 | Security | Low | Partially Verified | `Dockerfile:2` | The "python" image runs with "root" as the default user. Make sure it is safe here. | `FROM python:3.12-slim` | See tool message: The "python" image runs with "root" as the default user. Make sure it is safe here. |

_Collapsed to one row per (rule, suppression reason) pattern (repeated instances rolled into a count) - these are NOT shown as individual findings because each was matched against a known, documented false-positive pattern (the same patterns real tools solve with `per-file-ignores`/`nosec`)._

| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |

The captured value here is a known-safe constant (an auth-scheme name or an error-code whose value equals its own name), not a real secret. |
| S106 | Security | test_fixture_secret | 21 | `/work/repo/backend/tests/test_admin.py:199` (+20 more) | Hardcoded-secret-shaped literal found inside a test/fixture path (tests/, fixtures/, __tests__/, conftest.py, *.test.*, *.spec.*). Test constants of this shape are standard test fixtures, not real credentials, unless named with an explicit production-intent signal (e.g. 'prod_', 'real_', 'live_'), which this is not. |
| S101 | Security | test_assert | 403 | `/work/repo/backend/tests/test_admin.py:209` (+402 more) | Ruff S101 (assert-used) flags Python's `assert` statement because it is stripped when the interpreter runs with -O (optimized mode) - a real concern in production code. Inside test files, `assert` is the correct, standard mechanism pytest relies on. |

## Section 5: Engineering Observations

_LLM judgement beyond what tools detect (design, risk, testability). Confidence is the model's own estimate - treat as advisory._

| Area | Observation | Severity | Confidence |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| backend/app/services/auth.py | The JWT SECRET_KEY is assigned a hard-coded default string ('changeme-use-env-var-in-production-32chars+'). The current pattern silently falls back to this insecure default when the environment variable is absent; there is no startup guard that fails fast if the env-var is missing. In a containerised deployment this is a latent secret-exposure risk regardless of the inline comment. | high | high |
| frontend/eslint / tsconfig | Approximately 900 ESLint no-undef findings flag standard browser globals (window, document, localStorage, fetch, HTMLElement, setTimeout, setInterval, clearTimeout, clearInterval, navigator, URLSearchParams, Response, describe, it, expect, jest, beforeEach, afterEach). This pattern is diagnostic of the ESLint environment config lacking browser: true and the Jest test environment lacking the jest global scope declaration, rather than indicating actual undefined-variable bugs. The linting pipeline is effectively broken, masking genuine issues in the remaining signal. | high | high |
| backend/app/services/payments.py | All three gateway stub functions (_gateway_authorize, _gateway_capture, _gateway_refund) have parameters (amount, payment_method, gateway_reference) that are never read — they all return hard-coded mock dictionaries. Combined with the SonarQube S1172 findings for these same parameters, the payment integration is wholly un-implemented. A production deployment with this code would silently succeed all payments without contacting any gateway, constituting a critical business-logic gap. | high | high |
| Dockerfile | The image runs as root (no USER directive after the python:3.12-slim base) and uses COPY . . which copies the entire build context including .env files, local SQLite databases, __pycache__, and any secrets present in the developer workspace. A .dockerignore file is absent from the project structure. These two issues together create unnecessary attack surface and risk of accidental secret inclusion in distributed images. | high | high |
| backend/app/services/delivery.py — assign_delivery_agent | Ruff (C901) and SonarQube (S3776) independently flag assign_delivery_agent at cyclomatic complexity 16 and cognitive complexity 40, both well above the enforced thresholds. This function handles agent proximity filtering, candidate ranking, offer issuance, and assignment recording in a single body. The high complexity directly increases the probability of edge-case bugs in the business-critical delivery assignment path and makes the logic difficult to unit-test in isolation. | high | high |
| backend/app/services/ — list_restaurants, update_restaurant_profile, update_menu_item, issue_refund | Four additional service functions exceed the cognitive complexity ceiling: list_restaurants (33), update_restaurant_profile (27), update_menu_item (20), issue_refund (20). These are load-bearing functions in the browse, manager, and payment flows. The complexity is driven by inlined filtering pipelines, conditional field patches, and nested status-machine transitions that would benefit from extraction into helper methods. | medium | high |
| frontend/src/context/CartContext.tsx | SonarQube S6481 correctly identifies that the CartContext value object is constructed inline on every render without useMemo. Any state change anywhere in the CartProvider — including location pings or unrelated re-renders — will cause every cart consumer across the component tree to re-render. On a screen with many menu items this is a measurable UI performance regression. | medium | high |
| backend — FastAPI dependency injection pattern | All routers use the legacy db: Session = Depends(get_db) injection pattern. Ruff B008 flags this across the entire router layer (70+ occurrences), and SonarQube S8410 recommends migration to the Annotated[Session, Depends(get_db)] form standardised in FastAPI 0.95+. While the legacy form is functional, migrating to the Annotated pattern removes the B008 noise, enables better IDE support, and is the canonical path going forward. The scale of the change makes it a planned refactoring task rather than an emergency fix. | medium | high |
| backend — error message string duplication | SonarQube S1192 flags strings such as 'Order not found.', 'Cart not found.', 'User not found.', 'Restaurant not found.', and the cascade-action strings 'SET NULL' / 'users.id' each appearing 3–6 times across model and service files. This is not cosmetic: when an error message or FK action string needs to change, it must be changed consistently across all sites. Centralising these as module-level constants eliminates silent divergence. | medium | high |
| frontend — email validation regex | The pattern /^[^\s@]+@[^\s@]+\.[^\s@]+$/ appears verbatim in at least five distinct frontend files (OnboardRestaurantForm, AdminDashboardPage, ForgotPasswordPage, LoginPage, RegisterPage). SonarQube S8786 flags each as having super-linear backtracking. Beyond the ReDoS risk, the duplication means any correction must be applied in five places. The pattern should be extracted to a shared validation utility and replaced with a catastrophic-backtracking-free equivalent. | medium | high |
| backend/tests — test integrity | SonarQube S2699 identifies a test case in CheckoutPage.test.tsx that has no assertions at all ('navigates to order confirmation page after successful payment'). Additionally, over 30 test functions across the backend test suite assign results to local variables that are never subsequently read (F841), meaning the test exercises code but verifies nothing about the return value. SonarQube reports 0.0 % coverage, suggesting either the test suite is not wired into the CI coverage pipeline or tests are not being executed in a measured configuration. | medium | high |
| frontend — accessibility / ARIA | SonarQube surfaces a cluster of accessibility issues across multiple pages and components: <div> elements carrying role='dialog' instead of native <dialog>; <span> elements carrying role='status' instead of <output>; a <nav> element carrying role='tablist' (S6842); non-interactive <div> elements with mouse/keyboard event listeners (S6847); and two form <label> elements either not associated with a control or lacking accessible text (S6853). These compound to produce an application that fails screen-reader navigation and keyboard-only use. | medium | high |
| backend/app/services/admin.py — _record_refund_payment | The _record_refund_payment helper contains a bare except Exception: db.rollback() block that silently discards any database error during refund Payment creation. If the Payment model structure is incompatible, the function logs nothing and continues, leaving the dispute resolved in the Dispute table while the Payment table has no record of the refund. This silent divergence would cause accounting reconciliation failures. | medium | high |

## Section 7: Recommendations

_Prioritized actions for the Refactoring agent._

| Priority | Action |
| --- | --- |
| high | Harden the JWT SECRET_KEY: remove the hard-coded fallback default, add a startup assertion (or raise RuntimeError) that fails immediately if the JWT_SECRET_KEY environment variable is absent or matches the insecure placeholder. This must be deployed before any production release. |
| high | Fix the Dockerfile: add a non-root USER directive (e.g. adduser --disabled-password appuser), create a .dockerignore that excludes .env, *.db, __pycache__, .git, and node_modules, and replace COPY . . with a targeted COPY of only the application source needed at runtime. |
| high | Fix the frontend ESLint configuration: add env: { browser: true, jest: true } to the ESLint config (or the equivalent globals declarations), and ensure tsconfig.json includes 'dom' in the lib array. Re-run the linter after this change to reveal any genuine no-undef issues hidden in the current noise. |
| high | Implement the real payment gateway integration: replace the three stub functions (_gateway_authorize, _gateway_capture, _gateway_refund) with actual gateway calls (or a properly abstracted gateway interface with a clearly-named mock implementation). Remove the dead parameters from the stubs, or document them explicitly with a TODO referencing the gateway ticket. |
| high | Replace the bare except Exception: db.rollback() in _record_refund_payment with explicit error handling: catch the specific exception, log it at ERROR level, and surface it to the caller so that dispute resolution does not succeed silently when the refund Payment record cannot be persisted. |
| medium | Decompose assign_delivery_agent (complexity 40), list_restaurants (33), update_restaurant_profile (27), and update_menu_item (20) into focused helper methods. Each extraction should be covered by a unit test for the extracted helper to ensure the refactoring does not regress behaviour. |
| medium | Wrap the CartContext value construction in useMemo with the full dependency array before the Provider render in CartContext.tsx to prevent unnecessary re-renders across the entire cart consumer tree on unrelated state changes. |
| medium | Centralise the repeated email validation regex into a shared frontend utility module and replace all five inline occurrences. Use a catastrophic-backtracking-free equivalent (e.g. a simple /^[^@\s]+@[^@\s]+$/ or delegate entirely to the browser's built-in email input validation or a validated library). |
| medium | Centralise repeated error-message strings ('Order not found.', 'Cart not found.', etc.) and SQLAlchemy FK action strings ('SET NULL', 'users.id') into module-level constants in a shared errors.py / constants.py module, then replace all duplicate occurrences with the constant references. |
| medium | Audit the test suite: add at least one assertion to the 'navigates to order confirmation' test case, remove or complete the test functions that assign return values but never assert on them, and instrument the CI pipeline to measure and enforce a minimum coverage threshold. |
| medium | Address the ARIA/accessibility violations: replace <div role='dialog'> with native <dialog>, <span role='status'> / <div role='status'> with <output>, add for attributes to disconnected <label> elements, and remove keyboard/mouse event listeners from non-interactive elements (use <button> or <a> wrappers instead). |
| low | Run the Safe Auto-Fix phase (Phase 1–3) to bulk-modernise all UP035/UP045/UP006 typing imports, delete unused imports (F401) and unused local variables (F841), reformat overlong lines (E501), and simplify nested conditionals (SIM102/SIM105/SIM114/SIM117). These 1,400+ findings are all auto_fix: true and require no manual decision. |
| low | Plan a FastAPI Annotated dependency injection migration for all routers (B008 / SonarQube S8410). Migrate in router-by-router batches so each batch is reviewed and tested independently. Remove the now-redundant response_model= parameters on endpoints where the return type annotation already specifies the same schema (SonarQube S8409). |
